A devout Catholic, Vargas vowed to become a priest
when he grew up and to fight the perverse legions of evil

their own ends.

Vargas had been studying at the Boston Seminary
when Ryder approached him. Ryder actively recruited
Vargas, recognizing in him the dedication and stamina he
needed ina member of his "team." He persuaded the young
Puerto Rican to abandon his vocation and take up the rod
and staff with him. Vargas had become somewhat fed up
with the tedious rituals of the Church, anxious to get his
hands dirty cleaning up the world. Ryder gave him the
opportunity.

Moreover, Ryder showed Vargas a new and greater
threat to the human race: changelings. Asa mortal, Vargas
could not see past the mortal guises of the changelings he
would be hunting. Ryder enchanted Vargas and forced
him to look upon Ryder's own horrific faerie form. Then,
Ryder fell on his knees in a confessional pose to repent for
exposing his own evil. Vargas joined with the poor blighted
soul in seeking out and destroying other fae.

Escetla Smich (Nighc-Sky)

In the depths of the rain forest on Kaua'i there lives a
tribe of Black Furies dedicated to the conservation of
Hawai'i's natural resources. They are said to be behind the
closing of the Dole pineapple empire on Lana'i and battle
against the overall trend toward tourism as the primary
industry of the islands.

Night-Sky, so named for the tiny dots of white that
freckle her otherwise black coat, leads the tribe. She works
in Homid form at the Haleakala National Park and the
Kanepu'u Preserve on Maui and on the Kamokau Preserve
on Kaho'olawe, alongside human biologists and zoolo-
gists, in an attempt to protect the many endangered
animal and plant species that live there.

Night-Sky grew up knowing her Garou nature, but she
also knew that in order to get anywhere in the world, she
would have to educate herself. She earned her doctorate at
Colorado State in Forestry and Zoology. Upon graduation,
she felt lost, not knowing where to go. Her human parents
gave her an all-expenses-paid trip to Hawai'i as her gradua-
tion presentand that wasall she wrote. Assoonas Night-Sky
saw the abuse of nature upon the islands, she had her cause.

Geraldine "Geri Cravicz

Before her Awakening, Geri taught Cultural Psychol-
ogy at the University of Maryland. Geri isa Dreamspeaker.
She came to Hawai'i many years ago, having been "called"
there by spirits that came to her in a dream. The spirits
called her their link to the outside, asking her to pass their
stories to others like her.

In her late 40s, Geri lives in a small bungalow on the
beach near Ma'alaea Bay on Maui. She makes regular treks
up into Haleakala National Park to commune with the
spirits there. She and Estella Smith have developed an
uneasy friendship as a result of their meetings there. Geri
can see Estella's Garou nature in her aura, but Estella
remains completely unaware of Geri'sspecial abilities. She
does know, however, that they have one important thing
in common: a desire to protect and preserve Gaia. Also
unknown to Estella, Geri had a hand in many of the
accomplishments Estella claims for herself, including the
closing of the Dole pineapple operation.

A bit of a crotchety old cuss, Geri makes few friends.
Her cynical nature has chased away more potential friends
than most people will acquire in a lifetime. Leading a
rather solitary life, she only goes out on the town once a
month to O'ahu to visit "Fairytales," a bar owned by a
fascinating woman named Nahome. Geri finds the tales
she tells inspirational.

Although she needs little to survive, Geri supple-
ments her income by telling the fortunes of the few special
clients who can put up with her abrasive manners. They

arrange appointments with her, and the night before, Geri

speaks with her spirits to discover what she can say about
the client's situation. On rare occasions, she has saved a
client's life or fortune.

Ruch Anne Geldszein

In 1975, Ruth Anne's father divorced his wife to marry
the woman with whom he had been having an affair. He
immediately moved his new wife and his daughter to Hawai'i.
This devastated Ruth Anne's mother, who proceeded to kill
herself ina warm bath of her own blood. They never told Ruth
Anne, then 10 years old, the truth about her mother's death,
but Ruth Anne knew and grew to hate her new stepmother.

Ruth Anne began a long stretch of rebelliousness
aimed at her stepmother. She did the most heinous things
she could think of to torment the woman she blamed for
her mother's death. Her father sent her to therapy, to no
avail, and he eventually threatened to send her away.
ately, a change came over Ruth Anne, an out-
ward change. She treated her stepmother with respect and
kindness. They went shopping together. Ruth Anne's father
couldn't have been happier. But Ruth Anne had a plan.

In the guise of a picnic, Ruth Anne coaxed her
stepmother to the edge of a cliff high above the crashing
waves of the Pacific. Sharp rocks rose up like teeth from
the seething water. Ruth Anne intended to push her
stepmother over the edge. She set it up, luring the woman
into position. Unfortunately, things didn't quite turn out
as she had planned. The stepmother had her own ideas of
who should die. Ruth Anne found herself flying over the
edge before she knew what had hit her.

Fortunately for Ruth Anne, a kindly, rather powerful
wraith reaped her before anything more ugly could get to her.
This wraith, Robert Morton, took her under his wing and taught
her what she needed to know to survive in the Shadowlands.
Ruth Anne roams the island of O'ahu where she died.

The following three stories are designed to be used in
the Immortal Eyes: Shadows on the Hill storyline in
Hawai'i. They allow the characters to travel some of the
same roads that the companions did in the novel, Shadows
on the Hill, while not directly affecting the storyline or
mimicking the actions of Leigh and her companions. Each
story is written to be played by a certain archetypal group
of kith (Seelie, Unseelie or the heroes), but are open-ended
enough toallow the pl.

ers to play any character type with

minimum modifications to the storyline itself.

The three stories are nonlinear, and while they can be
played in sequence, they also can be used as introductions
to the setting, as chronicles ot as side trips for an estab-

lished troupe. The first story, "Echoes of Legend" is a side

adventure in which the players have the opportunity to

gh and her legendary companions (though any

rs new to Hawai'i may be substituted) amidst the
Hawai'ian fae — the Menehune. It allows the characters
todiscover more legends surrounding these strange change-
lings and is a more light-hearted adventure. The second,
"Welcome to the Jungle," is an introductory story to the
Shadow Court activities on the main island in the city of
Hilo. Itis designed fora group of Seelie characters who are
in Hawai'i either on vacation, as members of the Seelie
Court in Oahu, or for some other reason the Storyteller
can come up with. The story involvesa sequence of events


that eventually bring the characters to Lord Yrtalien's
freehold, into the very heart of the Shadow Court itself. It
does not fully explain any motivations or full personalities
ofany of the major players in the Shadow Court, but rather
sets the scene for further explorations. It allows the char-
acters to explore their own reactions to the discovery of
the full-blown Shadow Court, without discovering any of
the intimate details of Lord Yrtalien's plans. The third
story, "Reflections of the Mirror," is about deceit and
backstabbing. This story works best with a group of Unseelie
characters within Yrtalien's court; however, Seelie char-
acterscould be substituted with only marginal modifications
to the story. During this story the characters are ap-

proached by Glynnis who seeks their aid to retrieve a book

from Yrtalien's library. This adventure allows the charac-
ters to fully participate in the Shadow Court's darker side
and provides direct interaction with many of the main
characters in the court.

‘Cchoes of Legend'

"Every man's life is a fairy tale, written by God's
fingers.

— Hans Christian Anderson

"Echoes of Legend" is short adventure delving into
the life and legends of the Menehune. This story is
designed for Leigh and her companions, but any group of
Kithain who may have a reason to interact with the
Menehune would work just as well. The Storyteller will
have to arrange for the characters to become acquainted
with the Menehune. It is an introductory adventure,
designed for the players to explore the game and to become
more comfortable with their characters, but it also allows
the characters to explore the Glamour of the hidden
grottos in the Menehune island.

The Storyteller should take care to read over the
Menehune section of the book before playing and to inform
the players of any important customs their characters would
have been introduced to. The characters should be ac-
quainted with the chief, Makani; his daughter Lulani; and
the loremaster, Hamaia. Other Menehune may be intro-
duced at the Storyteller's option. Regardless, the characters
must be on good terms with at least these Menehune before
the adventure can begin. If the players are not playing the
companions, the Storyteller may wish to create another
introductory story, introducing the characters to the
Menehune an then proceeding with this story.

This is a light-hearted adventure, and the Storyteller
should make sure that the tone stays this way. It centers
around the retrieval of the legendary wedding bands of
chief Kaiau and the nymph Kaliandrana. The rings were


bestowed upon the pair by the dragon goddess Pele.

are made of plain white coral with pink coral des

one ring for the male and one for the female. Each band
allows the wearer to automatically know the location of
her lovemate, as well as the lovemate's emotional condi-
tion. These rings are legendary; the loremaster knows of
them, but not of their actual whereabouts.

The characters should not find the rings until the very
end of the story, allowing them an opportunity to explore
the area and become relaxed in the beautiful tropical
setting. The hunt for the rings should be the calm before
the storm. The Storyteller should also emphasize the fact
that these rings are a part of the Menehune's tradition and
legend, and unless the Storyteller wishes otherwise, the
rings should be returned to the Menehune.

Theme and CDood

"Echoes of Legend" is intended to be light hearted
and childlike in tone. A "sense 0' wonder" should be
evident throughout the adventure. The story should be
full of fun and adventure, not burdened by time con-
straints or any real danger. If the characters wish to wander
around the grotto and explore the jungles — let them. If
they w
make some up.

h to hear more stories from Hamaia or Kakui,

Don't be afraid to stray from the exact text of the
story. Ifthe characters start to get frustrated, possibly allow
the woodland dryad, Kukui, to drop a few rhymes here and
there to push them in the right direction. Allow them to
use the Soothsay arts to their full advantage. This should
be a magical adventure, not a desperate quest.

Background

The story takes place after Leigh and her companions
arrive in the village of the Hidden Treasure and havi

passed Makani's trial, declaring them honored guests. The
companions have been given their own house and have
been offered a place among the Menehune as visitors. The
companions have taken this time to explore; Valmont
sharing stories with Hamaia, Tor is watching over his
young granddaughter as she joins other Menehune creat-
ing leis, and Leigh is learning the customs and foods of this
culture.

If your players opt not play the heroes, this adventure
should take place after the characters have become firmly
They
akenly
stumbled upon the native changelings, or perhaps they

Menehune.

Scene One: Around the Scory

Poot

The characters have gathered to hear Hamaia tell one
of the Menehune legends. They, as well as many of the
other Menehune, are seated around the small pool ina the
center of the grotto. The waterfall cascades down into a
crystal-clear pool; multicolored fish swim lazily in the
peaceful waters. Hamaia seats himself on an island in the
middle of the pool, dressed in the traditional garb of the
Menehune: loincloth, leis and flowered bracelets. The
grotto is still, save for the mus sounds of the waterfall
in accompaniment to his voice.

Hamaia begins tale of Kaiau, an ancient chief of the
Menehune: "Kaiau was a strong alii, one in whom the
mana was strong. He was respected for his swift justice
toward evil and his kindness toward those deserving. He
was a man of great virtue and of even greater love for his
people.

"One night, as Kaiau was wandering alone amidst one
of the many grottos of the island, he spied a maiden more
breathtaking than any he had ever seen. Uncertain as to
what she was, he watched her movements and actions,
estimating her prowess as a warrior and her nature. Now,
Kaiau had the interest of his people in mind, but soon he
grew entranced by her. For several nights he stole away to
that secret grotto to watch the mysterious woman. Finally,
one night when the moon was full and Glamour was
strong, she looked up at Kaiau and smiled. In that one
smile, he was lost.

"They met secretly for many nights; she learned of his
world, and he learned of hers. Her name was Kaliandrana;
she was one of the spirits tied with the Earth — a nymph
— and the grotto in which he had dis
home. He feared his people would not understand her or

-overed her was her

would fear her instead of accepting her as his mate. Many
months passed, and both found themselves ill without
each other. Kaiau would return to find her listless at night,
while he remained distracted by day. Kaiau finally decided
that he was ali'i, and his people must a
a bride. His decision made, Kaiau brought Kaliandrana
back to this very village. The people accepted her well
enough, though not without some reservation.

pt his choice of

"Several nights after the couple publicly declared
their affections, they awoke to see a beautiful young
woman with flaming red hair standing before them.
Kaliandrana immediately bowed, recognizing this as Pele.
She quickly instructed Kaiau to do the same. Pele be-
stowed a set of perfect coral rings on the couple, saying this


was the symbol of her blessing of this match. She told them
thatas long as they both wore the rings, they would never
truly be parted. The very next day they swore oaths to one
another upon this very mound." Hamaia gestures to the
mound he is seated upon.

Hamaia continues, his voice falling in sorrow, "The
goddess Pele required her sacrifice. The Menehune had
chosen a mortal — a young, beautiful maiden — to serve
that purpose. The young woman went to her death will-
ingly, but this did not appear to fully please Pele. The
mighty dragon showed her anger by loosing her fierc
flame over the Earth. In fear, the Menehune turned
against what they didn't know and drew their weapons

gainst Kaliandrana. Kaiau tried to protect her as best he
could as they both fled to her hidden grotto, but the
goddess' displeasure could be felt throughout the land.
Once within the safety of her grotto, Kaliandrana drew
upon her own mana to heal her beloved, closing the fatal
wounds on his body. However, when she tried to heal
herself she found she had not enough mana left —she died
in her lover's arms.

"Kaiau never returned to the people who shunned his
true love. The magical rings were never found, though
many have sought them."

The lorekeeper ends the story here, answering ques-
tions anyone may have. He reveals that the nymph's
grotto is supposedly close to Hidden Treasures, but no one
knows where for certain. He should insinuate that per-
haps, if one of the mysterious Gallain could be found, they
might have more information, adding that no one else has
seen anymph. He also goes on to say thatany who find and
return the rings would be much honored among the
Menehune.

The story arouses the adventurous spirit of many of
the young Menehune and it is decided by the villagers that
a hunt should be formed to find the rings. For doing so
would bring much pleasure to Pele, and would favor the
village for years to come. The younger Menehune become
very excited at the thought of a treasure hunt and entreat
the players to help them find these relics of legend. Be

reful not to give out too much information, but defi-

nitely enough to tantalize the characters and to pique their

curiosity. They should want to participate in this treasure
hunt.

Scene Two: The Dunc Begins

The decision having been made to seek out these
ancient items of legend, several of the younger Menehune
pull outcrude mapsand begin trying tolocate Kaliandrana's

grotto. A treasure hunt is called, and the village bustles

with the activity of those preparing for the hunt. Lulani
will declare a hunt's feast, or lu au, at the end of the day —
the guest of honor being those who locate the rings.

Gradually, the elder Menehune begin to catch the
spirit of excitement and whisper among themselves how
pleased Pele would be if they could return her rings to her.
If they have not already chosen to do so, they entreat the
characters to assist in finding such great Menehune relics,
offering the assurance that such a task should be simple for
great heroes such as themselves.

It is here that the Storyteller should bait the charac-
ters into going to look for the rings.

You can emphasize the name of the hidden glen
Hidden Treasures, or appeal to some players' more greedy
nature, offering a different prize for locating the rings.
Some of the younger Menehune children may tease the
outlanders, challenging them to try and find the treasure.
The focus on this scene should be the anticipation of and
excitement about the hunt. Pure fun is on the wind, and
it is catching. Alternatively, the Storyteller could decide
that the Menehune insist that the characters join the
treasure hunt before performing some favor they have
asked of them — they may even go so far as to insist that
they find the rings themselves. This would certainly change
the tone of the adventure, but would be suitable fora group
of characters who would be unlikely to volunteer to join
the hunt.

If any of the characters think to try and use the
Soothsay Art in conjunction with the nature realm, they
will not receive a definite answer to where the rings are
located. They find they cannot scry on the rings them-
selves, but geta definite impression thatsomething chimeric
in origin lies to the north. Try as they might, they cannot
get a lock on the whereabouts of the chimeric item they

sense.

Scene One: A Duncan'
We Wit Go...

The characters set cheerfully off toward the north of
Hidden Treasures. The day is bright; the breeze is cool.
The characters travels for about an hour, through various
smaller areas, full of scenic waterfalls and lush vegetation.
The first place they come across is a small clearing in the
lush vegetation. There are flowers as high as their waist,
and the sweet scent of hyacinth is in the air. A small stream
gurgles nearby, offering its clear, cool water if they desire
it. Tall coconut trees reach to the sky in silent homage.


The glade is silent, save the singing of the colorful birds.
Finding nothing but the natural Glamour and peaceful-
ness, they continue onward.

Be sure to describe each area with vivid descriptions,
evoking all the senses. Here there are areas untouched by
mortals; small crystal-clear pools with tiny waterfalls emp-
tying into them, flowers as big as a child, the air itself
seeming to sing. If the characters choose to stop at any
point and explore, they will find a variety of birds and
pethaps even a lizard or two — but no rings or evidence of
anything fae. You should allow each of the characters to
explore whatever they wish, but be careful that you do not
lose their interest. If they appear to be becoming frus-
trated, have them come upon Kukui's grotto sooner. Use
this scene to foster roleplaying; allow the characters to get
abetter feel of who they are. They run across other treasure
hunters or the natural wildlife of the area. Laughter floats
on the windas the other Menehune race to locate the rings
or evidence of their existence.

They finally come upona grotto thatis larger than the
ones they have been in before. Here a waterfall, about 10
to 15 feet in height, pours into a crystal-clear pool. The
pool is about six feet at its deepest point. Beautiful tropical
flowers are everywhere, springing from around tree roots
and from between rocks. The grass is lush and soft. The
abundant vegetation has sealed this place off from outsid-
ers. The characters can almost feel the tangible Glamour
in this beautiful clearing. It appears empty.

Scene Two: CDeecing che Nymph

As the characters enter the glade, they become aware

of rustling from some of the surrounding trees. Further
investigation will yield nothing out of the ordinary. One of
the characters should spot Kukui first. He is watching the
party from behind the waterfall, trying to decide whether
they are friendly or trespassers. If the characters are de-
structive in any way, Kukui will use his powers to frighten
the characters off. If they appear friendly and nondestruc-
tive to the area, he will eventually step out of the waterfall
and introduce himself as Kukui, keeper of this grotto.
Kukui is hospitable to the characters, offering them
cool drink and fresh fruit. He is inquisitive about their
nature, for he has never seen such strange fae. He seems
especially intrigued if there is a pooka among them. He
will ask such a character if he can transform into the
animal he resembles. If any pooka chooses to show that
particular ability, Kukui will grow even more delighted
and share his own transforming abilities with the charac-
ters. Kukui thirsts for knowledge of these outworlders and
will talk with the characters as long as they wish. He will


tell them he is a nymph, tied to the land, and that this is
his grotto.

If the characters ask him about the legends of
Kaliandranaand Kaiau, his face will grow long. He will tell
the characters that she was hailed as one of the bravest of
their kind, but also one of the saddest. He affirms that the
stories are actually truth and not myth. In fact, he tended
to both of them when they fled from the village, ages ago.
He tried very hard to help both, but his healing waters
where not strong enough to protect them. His sadness
reaches out to the party, reminding them that reality and
Banality encroaches upon even the happiest pair, even if
you live as long as this nymph apparently has. After more
conversation, he will reveal that he may know where the
grotto is that they are looking for. He will offer to assist
them in their endeavor, but warns them that there are
strange things in this area to be careful of.

If the characters choose to accept his help, Kukui will
offer to show them the grotto. He is anxious to learn as
much as possible from these strangers, and relishes the
opportunity for interaction. He will become sad and
withdrawn if the characters do not wish his company

Kutun

You don't remember your first day or, rather, the day
you became aware of your nature — it was so longago. You
had sought refuge in this grotto from the time when you

were small. Its peacefulness and beauty called to you, sung

to you. There was something strangely familiar, yet out of
reach. You would work extremely fast during the day,
waiting for the chance to be free and run to your secret
place

You remember with perfect clarity the day
truly became aware. It was twilight, the light filtered
through the trees, the wind was a whisper upon your sk
You broke through into this beautiful grotto and suddenly
felt a deep kinship with the waterfall and the small pond
at its center. You could feel everything around you, as if
you were a part of the grotto itself — you could feel its pain,
but also the intense beauty of your own personal paradise.
You became aware that you were one of nature's chosen,
a nymph, and this was your glade.

It was to your glade that Kaiau and your elder,
Kaliandrana fled to when the Menehune showed their
fear. Kaliandra's grotto was too faraway, and she knew that
you would protect them. You tended their wounds and
tried to heal the scars left by those who did not understand.
You mourned her loss and wept with the land as one of her
daughter's passed into the land that gave her birth. You

swore to stay away from these strange brethren, but over

time you have gone against your own decree. You have
spent the last few decades tending to the land. You honed
your skills to live within the water, earth or the trees,
though your true form is within water. Many come to you
for refuge from the world's trouble, and you always gladly
sing a soft song for them. You are deeply afraid of these
strange people with their glittering boxes and their loud
disrespectful voices, though also compelled by them.

Special Abilities: Kukui's nature allows him some
abilities while within his grotto. He can meld with any of
the natural elements (tree, water, waterfall, earth), mak-
ing it seem like he is just disappearing into the object. He
can use his water to heal minor wounds at a cost of one


Glamour (this is only useful on characters whose Health
Level isat Wounded or less). His presence and grace would
compel normal mortals toward Kukui if he allowed himself
to be seen during one of their visits. He can command his
area to do small things, such as waters to swirl and tree
branches to rustle, should he wish to frighten off any
unwanted visitors. This is his glade, and thus he is the
ultimate master over it.

Image: Kukui takes on whatever elemental form he is
near. If he is in the water, he will appear to be translucent.
Everything will seem very fluid about his manner and his

If he arrives from his tree, his skin will app
barklike, his hair green. His most common seeming is of a
very attractive young man with greenish-brown hair and
very tanned skin. He moves with a fluid grace and watches
everything before speaking. His voice resembles water
flowing through a stream — very soft and musical.

Roleplaying Hints: This is your grotto. Everything
here is under your command, and you are safe here, as is
anyone you choose to harbor. The years have shown a
stripping away of your early fears of the Menehune, and
youhave become more curious about theirculture. Youare
willing to help those who ask for itand who show you their

incerity in their requests. You like jokes and speaking in
metaphors.

Assuming all has gone well with Kukui, the charac

ravelers" who steal the mana from the land. He will

Scene One: The Grocto

Kukui makes his way before the characters, seeming
tomelt through the underbrush. There is an air of urgency
about him, as if he is afraid to be away from his precious
home any longer than necessary. He will begin muttering
under his breath strange rhymes and The charac-

ters can begin to feel the air become almost tangible with
Glamour. Any changeling with high Banality will find the
Mists being virtually ripped away as they plunge deeper
and deeper into the heart of the jungle

Kukui stops suddenly, cocking his head to the side to
listen. He is in tune with nature enough to be able to hear
the music of the waterfalls and to feel the shift in the
breeze. He is attempting to feel the opening to the grotto.
Kaliandrana died a few centuries ago, and since then, the
tectonics of the island have shifted enough to plunge her
grotto underground. Shouting "Follow me!" he plunges
headlong into a hole in the side of what appears to be a
small hill. He disappears quickly into the depths. If the
characters take too long, he will clamber back out, mo-
tioning anxiously for them to follow him, and then duck
back under.

The characters will find the tunnel leading under-
ground to be damp, but not unpleasantly so. The air here
is fragrant with the scent of flowers. Fluorescent lichen
produces a dull glow, giving off soft yellow light. The
ground is hard-packed dirt; the walls are stone. It does not


appear that anything has touched this place ina very long
time. All the characters should become more and more
aware of the feeling of Glamour emanating from the area
ahead. Eventually, the tunnel opens into a large under-
ground grotto.

Scene Two: Mere
There Be Oragons!

Ko'leel the dragon will fall upon whoever enters the
grotto first. She will prepare to breath a column of chimeri-
cal fire if the characters do not first step back into the
passageway. If the entire group steps back into the passage-
way, she will remain hovering in front of them. She is the
guardian of the grotto and takes her job very seriously. She
is a creature of majestic beauty, but deadly in a fight.

The characters have two choices here — they can
fight the dragon or they can try to reason with her.
Depending on how long they choose to wait, Ko'leel may
take the initiative in speaking to them. She has the ability
to speak telepathically and will do so, asking them why
they disturb this area. Kukui will urge the characters to try
and reason with the dragon; after all, fighting a dragon is
no small feat. Even if the characters do attempt to reason
with the dragon she will not be a pushover — she is
adamant about not letting them into the grotto. After all,
she has been charged with the act of protecting it at all
costs and who knows what danger these strangers could
bring. The characters must come up with some reason, and
proof, why they should be allowed into the grotto. Perhaps
one of the characters can tell their story? An Unseelie
might try to charm and beguile the dragon, while a Seelie
may rely on honor. The Storyteller's key to roleplaying the
scene of allowing them entrance is not to give in too easily.

If the characters choose to fight the dragon, they will
find ita difficult task. Ko'leel takes her job very serious and
will put up a good fight. She will strafe the chasm with
chimerical fire. She will move with lightning speed to bite

or claw at the characters, attacking trolls, redcaps and
those with chimerical weapons first. She will attack one
character single-mindedly, and only once that one is
"dead" will she switch to the next target. Fighting this
dragon should be a difficult task — one in which the
dragon almost wins; the characters should only narrowly
be able to defeat her. Every character who partakes in her
destruction should gain two points of temporary Banality.

Scene Three: Rewards Well Given

The journey back to the Menehune village is an
uneventful one. Twilight is drawing near, and the bound-
aries between night and day are thin. If the characters
extend the invitation, Kukui will be reluctant to join them
in the village. Old fears die hard. However, after some
gentle persuasion, he will agree to accompany the party
back to Hidden Treasures. His banter will become more
subdued, and he will stick close to the person he has built
up the best rapport with.

The village is alight with torches sparkling yellow,
orange, blue and green. The drums are being played in a
joyous beat, and the scent of fresh pig can be smelled
wafting through the trees. All around the shouts of chil-
dren can be heard intermingled with the steady beat of the
fire-drums. As the characters draw nearer, they see fire-
dancers prancing around the fire to the beat of the drums.

A group of Menehune stands off to the side, spears
out. Contrary to the rest of the village, they have serious
looks on their faces. The are speaking in low voices, one
man pointing to the northern end of the village. These
people are part of the search party that was organized when
the companions did not return with all of the other
children. Chief Makani is worried — these people do not
know the ways of the island and could be in trouble. As
soon as the characters become visible in the village,
someone will shout, and many of the Menehune will run
over toward them.

The characters will be taken to the fire circle. There is
a mixture of awe, fear and wonder at Kukui's appearance,
but they do not make any moves against him. The drum-
mers will start up again, and the chanters will begin singing.
Once the feast has begun, the characters will be encouraged
to tell their story. There is fire-dancing and drumming.
Many wish to meet the Kukui, intrigued by his existence.

If the characters announce immediately that they
have located the rings, Hamaia and Chief Makani will
come forward, asking to view the rings. The characters
should give the rings to the chief. It should be evident that

the chief did not expect anyone to actually find the rings,
and Kuku
letting the characters tell the tale to the whole tribe. Kukui
should interject here and there, especially adding in the

appearance is an added bonus. Have fun

bit about the tourists.

The characters will be hailed as the "honored" at the
feast. They receive seats next to the chief and are served
first. Hamaia has many questions about Kukui, such as
where he lives, how he survives and validation of other
legends about nymphs. Several of the young men will ask
any female characters to dance, as many of the women will


ask the male characters — even Kukui. Frivolity and fun
should reign as the chief announces the rings are truly the
sacred rings of Kaliandrana and Kaiau. The story con-
cludes here, but is only the beginning of the character's
relationship with the Menehune.

‘Welcome to the Jungle

"Welcome to the Jungle" is a medium-length adven-
ture fora band of Seelie characters. Itisnotas light-hearted
as the first adventure, but does not have the levels of
treachery that are present in the last. It ends in a very
ambiguous manner, allowing the Storyteller to decide
which direction the characters should go next — whether
to the next adventure or back to Queen Aeron or Duke
Aeon to report their findings. The story runs a wide
gambit, beginning with the discovery of strange chimeri-
cal beasts running about freely and leading to the discovery
of the Shadow Court and Lord Yrtalien's freehold. This
adventure allows the characters to test their investigative
prowess as they discover what or who is behind a rash of
strange events.

This story is designed to introduce Seelie characters
to the Shadow Court. Unseelie who are not aware of the
court's existence may also be integrated in this s
little difficulty. One of the Seelie options for this story is
for the players to be members of Count Menihiron's court.
They could have been sent to the city of Hilo to discover
the truth behind some strange rumors of a new sidhe lord
in the city and to offer greeting from the count. Alterna-
tively, the players could just be on vacation to the beautiful
islands, seeking refuge from a world laden down with
Banality. If your players choose to play the companions,
you can use this as a means of introduction to Lord
Yrtalien, rather than mirror the series of events found in
the novel.

Theme

As the title signifies, "Welcome to the Jungle" is an
introduction to the excesses and the wickedness of the
Shadow Court. Here they use Glamour freely and without
consequence. The philosophy of this court is that mortals
are the servants to the Kithain and should be treated as
such. Yrtalien has several enchanted mortals within his
freehold, their only purpose being to please him. Mortals
are beneath those who wield Glamour, and to show
anything but superiority toward them is considered being
soft which the court finds distasteful. These are the true
Unseelie, and they are proud of their new court.

These things should feel wrong to the players. They
should not fall into the ways of the Shadow Court, until

perhaps the end. They need to recognize that while


Hawai'i is a natural resource of Glamour, it is being torn
from the land at an alarming rate. If this continues to
occur, Hawai'i will eventually end up just another tourist
trap, devoid of all but the most superficial of Glamour.

(Dood

This story should be reminiscent of a traditional
gothic novel; like Jane Eyre or Emily Bronté. In the
beginning of the story, things are normal enough and life
is bright. The characters are ina city suffused with beauty,
fun and Glamour. Gradually, strangeness enters the
character's life, pulling them into the unknown. The
horror should mount as some of the stronger examples of
the Shadow Court are discovered, such as the ravaged
islanders. What's more, there are those out there who
know of these travesties, but are not doing anything about
it! How can this be?

Thestory should end witha feeling of dread and horror
at the ultimate discovery — the Shadow Court itself!

Background

This story can take place a few days after the first
adventure or within a few days of the characters' arrival in
the city of Hilo. The city of Hilo is beautiful and free of all
but the most rudimentary forms of Banality. There is a
feeling of wonder in the air, and that can be seen in the
beautiful handcrafted items of the islanders. The city is full

of gift shops that are manned by natives who make small

items to buy. Every night a lu'au can be found, and during
the day there are the beautiful gardens to behold or the
sparkling beach to explore.

It is only a perhaps a week since Prince Yrtalien
stepped on the island and created his freehold. The party is
just now in full swing. He has given Siva her title, and all of
the Unseelie mentioned in Chapter Five are in attendance.

Acc One: CDonscers,

CDonscers, Everywhere
Scene One: On che Town

Hawai'i is a place of magic, a refuge from the world's
Banality. It is a place where the world's Banality is held at
bay and the Kithain can truly feel free. Here grumps do not
need to fear the Mists as much as they don the mainland.
The shops are filled with handmade items, beautiful leis
and shells galore. Here there are nightclubs that stay open
late, and you can find a lu'au almost every night


The scene begins with the characters strolling down
the street toward the club, Reflections. The Storyteller
will have to inventa reason for them to go here — perhaps
they have heard the wonderful international reviews of the
restaurant and have decided to try its cuisine on their own.
Reflections is a well-to-do restaurant club that offers
both fine dining and dancing and is one of the most
popular restaurants in the city. It is located below street
level, and next to a pond filled with Japanese koi fish, on
Aupuni street. The characters have heard only good
things about itand are anxiously waiting to sample the fine
cuisine and wonderful music. It is a beautiful I
night; the skies are clear, there isa faint breeze blowing the
It smell from the ocean, and the colorful birds

wai'ian

wonderful
of the island walk freely about. There are hundred of
tourists walking happily about; lovers walking hand in
hand, children running ahead of their parents only to
scamper back to their families' familiar grasp.

The characters arrive at the club with relatively little
problem, walk down the winding stairs to enter and are seated
together around a table near a set of bird cages. There is soft
music playing in the background, and people are dancing on
the dance floor located down another short flight of steps.
They can order a variety of foods, both Continental and
American fare. Dinner isserved, and the characters should be
enjoying each other's company when a commotion can be
heard from a small bridge over one part of the large pond.

If the characters do not immediately investigate, they
may be inclined to when the woman grabs her son's hand
and pulls him off the bridge, shouting something about
contaminated water or illegal fish in the restaurant. Other
patrons may have their curiosity peaked and wander over
to look in the water. Many stare in strange fascination,
while others turn away pale.

The characters move over to see what everyone is
talking about and view a very large chimerical fish. It is
slowly eating all of the other fish in the pond, leaving a
trail of blood through the pond. It has a tendency to
unnervingly turn and smile at the nearest person, displa
inga large mouthful of razor-sharp teeth. When itspies the
characters, its eyes narrow and it get a very predatory look
on its face. It rises out of the water, and flies out of the club.
Shouts of "flying fish," and screams can be heard from
outside the restaurant.

Scene Two: The Chase 1s On

Hopefully the characters will abandon their food and
take off after the chimerical beast. If they do not do so
immediately, the Storyteller should provide some incentive.
Perhaps the chimera attacks several of the restaurant patrons
before fleeing, and if nothing else, they should be curious as
to how the mortals present are able to see the chimera.

Assuming all goes as planned, they charge up the
stairs to find several fainted mortals and several others
with dazed looks on their faces. If anyone stops to ask, the
people will point down the street and toward Hilo Bay.
Faint screams can be heard coming from that direction.

The characters should pursue the chimera down the
street and toward Hilo Bay. They can follow the steady
stream of colored ichor or the stunned look on people's
faces as a fish the size of a dog soars by in the air. The fish
will fly through houses and cut over a few streets, leaving
confused people in its wake. It will fly between people's
legs and through jungle gym equipment, forcing the char-
acters to dodge around and about. As it flies, it seems to
have no motive except chaos. They will catch glimpses of
it rounding corners, going through windows, etc. This
should resemble, in a comic way, a car chase one would see
on TV. The fish will finally turn into what appears to be
adead end alley. In truth, the fish is leading them into an
ambush.

Scene Three: Inco the Alleywiay

As the characters turn the corner into the alleyway,
several things will be noted at once. The alleyway is, in
fact, a dead end. Two large buildings loom on either side,
no windows or doors facing into the alley. No fire escapes
are evident on either building.

The fish stops, hovering at the end of the alley. It is
smiling at the characters in a very unsettling manner. The
characters should begin to feel uneasy; here they are, in an
alley, with a large chimerical fish, and the fish isn't doing
anything but smiling. The Storyteller should really take
this opportunity to build up the feeling of suspense and the
bitter edge of fear. Something is wrong.

A Perception + Alertness check (difficulty 7) may
alert the characters to the other two chimera before they
attack from behind, though any characters watching their

ks will notice them immediately. In fact, this was one
big set up. These three chimera are recently escaped from
Lord Yrtalien's garden hunt and are out to do the thing
they do best — hunt. Each one was summoned to chal-
lenge the more daring of Unseelie, complete with their
own set of natural weapons. Pug looks much like a large
wad of Silly Putty; his skin is ruddy pink, and his body
squat. The other chimera looks like a gremlin with a
greenish-black scaly hide and tail. The two new chimera
will not waste a moment before attacking the characters,
reacting swiftly and without mercy. Their statistics can be
located at the end of this scene.

Pug and the gremlin will use chimerical swords to
attack the characters, while the fish will fly about and use

Kater Fash

This fish is about the size of a medium-size dog with
the personality of a rabid Doberman. It was summoned to
amuse those who wanted to go fishing, but had an added
twist. It doesn't need water to survive, and it can fly. The
huge green-scaled body looks normal at first for an exotic
fish — its fins are an array of iridescent colors, it moves
lazily through water — but when one looks closer, one sees
other, disturbing things. Its eyes are pure silver, lined with
red. Its mouth contains two rows of razor-sharp teeth
capable of biting through bone, and it has a smile capable
of unnerving even the boldest troll.

Immorcal Cyes: Shadows on che hi

It is a strict carnivore and requires large amounts of
raw meat (chimerical meat that is). Because of this fact, it
strayed to the first area it could find where it could possibly
blend in. In its mind, it has only one mission: find food —
preferably Kithain (though other chimera will do in a
pinch). What better place to wait for an opportunity but
at a restaurant? It agreed to work with the other renegade
chimera in the hope of providing amusement for their own
sake, not for the sake of others. In reality, she has little to
no loyalty to either Pug or the gremlin. She will eat them
too if she gets hungry enough.

Pug

Pug is best described as a bipedal form of putty. While
he does have two legs, two arms and a sort of face, his skin
color is ruddy pink and his entire body is supported by
cartilage. He resembles a cartoon character, though a
rather repulsive one. His eyes are buglike and he has no
hair, save big, bushy, black eyebrows. He stands only three
feet tall, but carries a very large chimerical ax.

Pug has the unique ability to shift his body whichever
way he wishes, as longas he keeps his full body intact. That
is, he cannot split apart, like an amoeba, or in half. He can
shift himself over and around a person's face, or other body

part, squeezing and cutting off circulation. He has no real

higher thought processes besides to kill and thus follows
the fish and the gremlin without question.

His escape from the freehold's garden was really a
fluke. He was one of the medium-danger chimera created,
but he stumbled onto the gremlin in the maze. The
gremlin, amused by Pug's horrible appearance, brought
him along when he escaped into the city. He is, by far, the
easiest of things to kill.

Attributes: Strength 2, Dexterity 5, Stamina 3,
Charisma 2, Manipulation 1, Appearance 1, Percep-
tion 1, Intelligence 1, Wits 3

Glamour: 5, Willpower: 2

Gremlin

The gremlin is a fierce, war-oriented creature. His
body is covered with a green-black hide that makes it
difficult to hit him with normal weapons. His streamlined,
erpent-like shape allows him to dart and move
quickly, and his short height allows him to dart between

almost

legs and through tunnels. Like the fish, he has razor-sharp
teeth, but h
tail. His eyes reflect yellow in the light, scaring any mortal

so has a pair of wicked claws, and a lashing

who might see him.

His favorite method of attack is to lay low and blend
with the surroundings. He then springs out and hamstrings
his victim or severs the person's Achilles tendon, render-
ing them unable to do anything but crawl. Then and only
then will he move in and very sadistically carve up the
poor victim. He consumes the flesh of the Kithain, causing
him to gain extra Health Levels. His blood is like acid and
if touched will cause aggravated real damage. He is profi-
cient at using his claws and tail. He is a devious, evil
creature and should be the most difficult of all to kill.

Powers

* Acidic blood — His blood is much like that of the
creatures in Aliens. When he bleeds, it eats through

blood must either wipe is off or find some other way of
removing it. The blood does three soakable Health Levels
the first round, and one additional level per round that the

* Chimerical Claws — His claws are far more deadly
than most, as they rend the very fabric of your chimerical
existence from you. With each successful attack, the
character must make a successful soak roll lest the Gremlin
rend the Glamour from her soul. For each successful attack
that does damage, the character looses one temporary
Glamour point. It should be described in such a way that
the player is fully aware of what is happening.

© Consumption — By eating his victim, the Gremlin
can either heala number of wounds equal to half the victim's
available Health Levels (for Kithain, 7), or he may add those
levels to his own Health Levels, increasing the amount of
damage he can take. For example, if Gremlin consumes
Mary, a childling eshu, he will have the choice of healing 3
wounds or adding 3 Health Levels to his total pool.

Chapzer Seven: Scenes


Growing up in Sacramento, California, was rough.

Michael's mother endured his father's abuse, and he silently

took it each day, letting his anger grow within him. His

father quickly squelched all the fairy tales, and he came to

realize at an early age that things like Santa Claus, the

Tooth Fairy and the Easter Bunny where just cruel jokes

played on gullible kids. Well, he wasn't gullible, He was
strong, and he wrapped his anger around him like a blanket.

Michael zoomed through high school, acing most

courses and still making the varsity football team. He was

a large, good-looking man, but his abrasive disposition
prevented him from having any long-term relationships.
Secretly, he was afraid he might become too much like his
father and end up hurting someone he loved. When his
father threatened to throw him out at age 18, he gladly
packed up his bag and left. He went far away and flew to
Washington, D.C., and to Quantico. He had decided to
become a federal marshal.

This new obsession to bring the scumbags like his

father to justice drove him. He worked his way through

college and got accepted into the federal marshal's pro-

gram. He persevered and was hailed as one of the top

members of his class, winning his choice of assignments.

He choose the opposite end of the states from his family;
he went to New York City.

It was here that he met the one woman who could
make him laugh: Kate Rollins. They met, strangely enough,
in a bookstore where she bumped into him, spilling her

Michael will take the characters to a small house on

If they choose the stakeout, they will find the address
that Wyvern gave them to be correct; it is a large house, set
back on the hill. To mortals, it seems like a run-down,
dilapidated house, but to the character's eyes it is a glorious
mansion in its prime. Laughter can be heard drifting down
the hill mingling with screams — from what it isnot known.

The characters can sneak up the hill, making successful
Dexterity + Stealth (Difficulty 7) rolls. Looking in windows
they will see a variety of things; all Unseelie. They will see
Siva, the satyr that Yrtalien made into a noble, kissing and
groping another satyr in one corner of the room. They will
seenumerouspeopledrinkingand laughing, throwing Glam-
our around like it was free. They may catch a glimpse of
Devlin or Tor. Any of Leigh's companions would be alone.
Edmund will be seen enjoying eating everything and any-
thing possible. Tor and Morgan would be looking extremely
out of place. Rasputin will be seen with a large troll; her
name is Diana. However long the characters remain, they
should adequately feel the opulence and debauchery. Michael
willlook faintly ill at the levels of it. Ifthe characters stay too
long or make too much noise, two large troll bouncers will
arrive and bring them inside.

Scene Live: The CDeecing

Whether by being caught or by willingly going into
the freehold, the characters should visit the freehold itself.
If they are being brought in by the bouncers, they will be
immediately shown to Prince Yrtalien. If they are coming
in of their own accord, Lord Devlin will great them. He
does not appear to recognize the characters, though they
are very certain he is the one who Ravaged the owner of
the Aloha Shop.

They will be brought in and welcomed cordially. Wine
filled with dross will be offered. They will be told about the
hunting grounds in the gardens and told that if they desire
weapons to help with the hunting, they have but to ask.
Several satyrs will come and make advances on the charac
ters, making insinuations and cooing innuendo. Many are
especially interested in Michael, who is standing, jaws
clenched. This is an opportunity to meet any of the com-
panions if you wish to have your characters meet them.
They haveall been very deliberately separated, and thus the
characters would not meet more than one or two ata time.

After some time, Prince Yrtalien will send for them.
He is'a very charming man who exudes a very tangible
presence. He will answer any of the characters' questions,
proclaiming to be the Unseelie Prince and to have just
come from Arcadia itself! He will offer a place for the


characters within hisnew ranks, confidentthat the Unseelie
will sweep over Concordi

After thismeeting, the characters have several choices.

d find more information about
Yrtalien, or they can leave and tell Queen Aeron of
Kingdom Pacifica. Ifany character chooses to stay and join
the courts, he will be rewarded highly, but everything has
a definite price. Prince Yrtalien has one main object
Bringing about the return of the true Shadow Court — he
truly intends to do it. This adventure should leave the
characters ina very ambiguousstate. Do they have enough
information to tell Queen Aeron? Should they further
pursue the court? This would be a good start toa chronicle
set in Hawai'i for Seelie. How will Count Menihiron's
court react? What should the characters do?

Possible Followups

The characters travel to Queen Aeron to inform her
of Yrtalien's presence in Hilo. Upon arriving, you are
taken aside by another man and warned against speaking
about the court. Who is he, and what does this mean?

The characters travel to Menihiron's court to inform
him of Yrtalien's presence, but discover Unseelie within
his own court. How should they handle this? Should they
try to uncover how large the Unseelie following is in
Hawai'i? Or just leave it lie?

Michael begins recognizing many of the missing teen-
agers and young adults around the freehold. His ire raises;
he entreats the characters to assist him in freeing them
from Yrtalien's enchantments.

The next adventure, "Reflections on a Mirror", is a
suitable follow-up for any Unseelie or Seelie oathcircles.

The characters try to leave this scene behind, appalled
that a Shadow Court of this size has gone unnoticed by any
of the nobles. They are disillusioned, but want nothing to
do with the politics of court. Have them stumble upon a
cold iron knife shipment to another city — courtesy of
Lord Yrtalien. Glynnis and Yrtalien plan to havea reenact-
ment of the Iron Knives Massacre — this time Seelie
against Unseelie. What should the characters do?

"Temptation—

Why won't you leave me alone?
Lurking Every Corner, Everywhere I go
Self Control —

Don't turn your back on me now


When I need you most

Constant pressures test my will"

— Dream Theater, "The Mirror"

"Reflections on the Mirror" is the third of these stories
set in Hawai'i. While "Echoes of Legend" is a bright,
cheerful story and "Welcome to the Jungle" is like a super-
natural mystery, "Reflections on the Mirror" begins with a
dark and sinister nature that transports one to a realm of
backstabbing and corruption. The story revolves around
Lord Yrtalien's assistant, Glynnis, entreating the characters
to acquire several books. Though the characters may think
they are doing the right thing by assisting Glynnis, they will
quickly find themselves pawns ona large chessboard. Their
assistance will give them the sense of power and in turn
unwittingly allow themselves to be corrupted.

This is a story meant for Unseelie characters who are
freely interacting in the new Shadow Court. Conse-
quently, the Storyteller should make sure she has a good
handle on all the characters' motives in the Unseelie
Court. If the characters are Seelie, this adventure should
be very uncomfortable for them. If the characters went
through the "Welcome to the Jungle" adventure, this
should definitely precipitate the characters' going and
getting help from Queen Aeron.

Theme

"Reflections on the Mirror" is all about the deceitful
and underhanded ways of the Shadow Court. There are
forces beyond the characters' control who use them for
their own means. Beneath all the frivolity and antics,
there is power, and power corrupts. Power gives the ability
to dub someone a noble. Power emboldens the Shadow
Court, and with enough power, the Shadow Court can
overthrow the Seelie Court. Whoever possesses the Im-
mortal Eyes is the one with the power, and there are those
who will do anything to possess them — without even
knowing what they do. Asked to retrieve certain books
and diaries from Prince lien's library and bedroom, the
characters will discover they are not removed from this
power play. Should they give the books to Glynnis? Or
should they try to gamer favor from Prince Yrtalien? It will
ultimately be their decision what they will do with the
knowledge they possess.

The characters should feel the heady rush of power as
they learn some of the potential the Immortal Eyes possess.
Power has its price though. Will they dare to defy Prince
Yrtalien and be destroyed by him, or will they willingly
deliver the information to Glynnis? It is a dangerous road
the characters go down, and they should tread carefully.
This story is about passion, deceit and desire for the
ultimate tool — The Immortal Eyes.

Immorcal Cyes: Shadows on che hut


(Dood

A wild party is taking place in the haunted house on
the hill in Hilo, but the party has a very different atmo-
sphere than you might expect from it. There is an endles
supply ofalcohol, Glamourand sex, but underneath all the
wealth and frivolity, there is a dark shadow looming over
everything. This shadow lies in wait to remind he who
came and usurped her power with her own of her own
desires. She wants his power, and she will do anything to
get it. The characters are naught but pawns in this power
play. Whose pawn will they ultimately be? Their own,
Yrtalien's or Glynnis'?

The mood of this story is very dark, filled with
nebulous choices and grim temptations. Even Unseelie
should feel the cold clutches, not of Banality, but of
duplicity. Who can be trusted when you possess items of
power or the knowledge behind such items? You must
tread carefully, for who knows who will betray whom.
Each character will have to make the choice of with whom.
they are going to share the knowledge they have obtained,
or will they use it to their own benefit? Trying to obtain the
Eyestones themselves will lead to their destruction, but
trying to help Yrtalien or Glynnis consolidate her power
may lead to wealth. Which way to go?

Background

This story takes place after Leigh and her compan-
ions have arrived at the Shadow Court. The Court itself
has been in full swing for about a month. In that time,
Prince Yrtalien has shared news that he hails from Arcadia
and that he plans to bring the Shadow Court back to its
full, real power. Too long has the Shadow Court been
merely a farce, not the true beauty of what it is in Arcadia.
He has called to the Unseelie of Concordia to join him in
his newfound Court, and many have flocked to be with
him. Yrtalien wields his power like a true Lord. He names
tulers on whims, and all the Unseelie love him — or do
they?

Glynis secretly despises the way he has come in and
taken over what she had spent a good amount of time
working on. She no longer leads the Unseelie forces in
Oakmont, but is rather Prince Yrtalien's consort. He
wields the power she, by right, should have. He does not
acknowledge all she has done forhim— the people she has
brought together, the freehold she established. He wields
the power of the Shadow Stone, but she desires it. She has
been watching Yrtalien, trying to ascertain all the Shadow
Stone's powers, and has been waiting for the chance to
make her own move in this large chess game.

As the characters leave the library, they are followed
outside by Callie. She hands them a note, curtsying,
telling the group, "I was asked to give you this." She will
wait for the members to open it, in case there are any
further orders. The characters open the parchment and

The characters should be given a short amount of
time to discuss the note among themselves and tell Callie
their answer. If they decline, Callie will flinch, but nod
accordingly. If they accept, she will curtsy politely and

walk off toward the study. Ifthe characters decline, Glynnis
will find them together at some point later that evening.
She will approach them discreetly, clearly not wish-
ing to meet in the open. She will lead the characters to a
enclosed part of the garden, away from the rest of the
freehold. Chimerical creatures can be seen darting about
the foliage every few minutes, but no other Kithain follow.
Turning to the party, she offers a genuine smile, asking
them first how they are enjoying their stay and making
small talk. After a few minutes, her voice will lower
slightly, and she will ask the characters' views on Prins
Yrtalien. If they respond positively towards Yrtalien, she
will take her second approach and will gently turn the
She will
make claims that she left a book in his room and needs it
back. Lady Glynnis will make the pretense of feeling very
embarrassed by the situation, looking down frequently,

The diary will have the sort of information needed to find

requires to help put this so-called prince in place. She needs
someone else to get the books, for she spends most of her
time under his watchful eyes. She will explain that Lord
Devlin is enchanted by him and cannot be trusted, as are
most of the people in the freehold. The characters alone can
retrieve the needed evidence to dispense of this farce.

In actuality, Glynnis wants the book and diary for
very different reasons. She knows the Eyestones are in-
credibly powerful, but nothing else. She is certain there is
information within those books that will allow her to
possess the gems for herself and claim the title to the
Shadow Court. In the end, she will call upon them to
perform their duty as Unseelie to assist her. If that fails, she
will offer the characters any sum to retrieve the book and
the diary from Prince Yrtalien. Power, dross, chimerical
weapons and armor — nothing is too small of a price for
the items she desires. She figures, if she has the knowledge,
she can get the gem and put Yrtalien in his proper place.

If the characters are Seelie, Glynnis will first try to buy
them off with power—anything their heart desires. Barring
that, she will attempt to blackmail them with the fact that
they have been participating in Unseelie decadence.

Scene Three: The Bedroom

The characters have a series of choices in attempting
to' gain entry into Lord Yrtalien's chambers. There is a


cantrip lock on the door, requiring a certain set of notes to
be whistled. The area around the chamber is frequented by
the other nobles, and though there are two entrances to the
wing, the nobles only go up the main staircase. If the
characters choose not to engage Callie's assistance, the next
few steps will still occur in the same order. Other enchanted
and Kithain know the key, including Glynis and Siva.
Callie takes the characters through a back staircase to
the east wing of the mansion, seeming fearful. The air isstill,
almost tangible as she walks, moving quickly through the
archway into the spiraling staircase. Only candlelight or
Glamour lights the way, sending flickers along the wall and
shaping phantom monsters. As the characters reach the top
of the staircase, she hushes them. "This is where Prince
Yrtalien and his nobles live. Lady Siva, Lord Devlin and
Lady Glynnisall have rooms on this hall." She peeks around
the corner and then pulls back as she hears Lord Devlin
speaking with someone in the hallway. There is a silence as
footsteps can be heard coming towards the stairwell, only to
turn back as his partner cajoles him to bed. A door opens
and shuts, their voices fading with the door's closure.
The hallway is larger, seeming more like a cavern than
the standard hallway the characters traversed through be-
fore. The feeling of being watched intensifiesas they approach
aset of large oak double doors. If any of the characters reach
forth to open the door, Callie brushes the hand away
quickly, explaining there is a key. She opens the door,
humming a small song. The doors open into a large, very
opulent room that takes up the full side of the hall. There is
ahuge king-size four-poster bed in the center of the room, its
head against the wall on the left. It is covered with pillows
and blankets, all black. A large oak desk sits against the left
wall, the roll-top pulled down over the desk itself. There is
a small bookcase next to it. A pair of high-back leather

chairs face the fireplace, but are spaced far apart. There are

several prints on the wall, varying from Escher to an Impres-
sionist to erotic art. The bed looks like it has been slept in
recently, and the tangy smell of sweat hangs in the air.
Callie stands right inside the door, as if afraid to go
into the room any further. She points to the desk, saying,
"[ think the stuff is in there." The characters may go to the
desk and investigate it. Much of the same items are re-
vealed: letters, stamps, fine parchment paper, sealing wax
but no seal, and an ink well. A successful Perception +
Alertness roll (Difficulty 9) will reveal a small compart-
ment on the side of the desk. Glamour hides it well, and
there seems to be some sort of cantrip key needed to open
it. Any character with Prop 2 and Legerdemain 1 may try
and open it via using a cantrip. The characters can work
together to Gimmix open this panel. Brute force will also
work, but the seal will be broken, and Yrtalien will be aware


of who broke it. Once this has been done, the characters
retrieve a single, leather-bound book. Checking inside,
they find it is indeed Prince Yrtalien's diary. They do not,
however, find any books with the word eyes in the title.

The characters can search around the room foras long
as they wish. They find little of interest, save a chimerical
cube with a picture of the prince and Leigh together in
some land with huge crystal spires in the background.
They seem to be very friendly toward each other. After
some period of time, some character should stumble upon
the book, The Immortal Eyes of SanGrane. Further investi-
gation yields it is a mythology book about some tiger
eye-gems that are reputed to have some magical healing
abilities tied in with immortality. There is little else in it,
but it is the book that Glynnis requested.

As the characters are inspecting the room, the sung
keycan be heard outside the door. The characters have but
a few seconds before a young, attractive satyr enters the
room. She stops as she enters the room, door on handle,
and looks cautiously curious. She will ask, "Hello, my
name is Kree. Now what in the world are you doing here?"
The characters must explain why they are present in the
prince's room. If they are having a hard time, Callie will
interject at the last possible moment that they are here on
the prince's request, retrieving some items for later. Either
way, it doesn't take much to convince Kree to leave.

Immorcal Cyes: Shadows on che hut

Her interruption should serve asa warning and should
intensify the mood. They should be reminded that they are
in the prince's bedroom and that should he see them,
unpleasant things will occur. Callie will seem very nervous
after she leaves, urging the characters to move as quickly
as possible. She will only seem relieved once they leave the
room with the two books.

Acc Three: Oecisions

Scene One: (Deering in che
Courtyard

The characters now have the books they were asked to

retrieve. Callie will sneak them downstairs, and then inform
them she will tell the Lady they wish to speak with her. She
will seem confused if any character contradicts her, but will
acquiesce to their wishes. The characters return to the small
enclave in the garden. Once more the sounds of the party fade
in the background, and the characters find themselves alone.
They have in their possession Prince Yrtalien's diary and the
book. They have to decide what to do next.

If any character begins reading the journal, allow the
player to read the entries at the end of the story. Closer
inspection of the Immortal Eyes shows it to be nothing more
thana Scandinavian mythology book and of no great import.


The characters should be very confused as to why Glynis
would want it. The characters should be allowed as much
time as possible to decide what they wish to do. They are
fairly certain that confronting Yrtalien would be unhealthy
for the strongest of their group. They have no idea what the
references to the stones are and do not care who Kanani is.

If the characters decide to try and find Leigh, she will
always be with either Yrtalien or another member of her
own oathcircle.

Scene Two: Trapped in the

CDiddle

Unless the characters move quickly tofind Prince Yrtalien,
Glynnis will find them within an hour. Callie has alerted her
to their possession of the books and of where they are in the
freehold. She walks in on the characters with a friendly air as
they are talking, and greets them. She will ask for reaffirma-
tion about the acquisition of the books, standing very poised
and silent. Callie cowers in her shadow, seeming to look over
her shoulder every so often. The characters should respond to
her however they deem fit, but ifthey seem to be stalling, Lady
Glynnis will begin to get miffed and demand the books.

The characters should notice a shadow walking up
behind Glynnis. Callie seems fearful, more so than before,
and Lady Glynnis does not appear to notice. Prince Yrtalien
will step out from the shadows, tsking, "Glynnis, your power
would come in time. I do not take kindly to this deceit. You
forget yourself." Glynnis's face will go white as Prince
Yrtalien will make it seem as if she is in a pool of hot lava.
He will turn to the characters and ask them politely, "Now,
what are you doing with my journal and my book?" He does
not look angry, which alone should unsettle most if not all
of the characters. He will wait patiently for their reply. He
willacceptnothingshort of the truth. Ifany character begins
tolie to him, save a pooka, he will begin to torture them with
cantrips, reminding them that he is the lord of this freehold.

If the characters tell everything, from beginning to
end, he will show leniency toward the characters, possibly
even rewarding them for such honesty. If any character is
willing to flourish the story enough to make Lady Glynis
extremely bad, the prince will consider giving the person
a title as a reward. He is aware of Glynnis's desire to take
from him this power and has been watching for any signs
of underhandedness. He will allow the characters to go
with a minimum amount of pain or anger, though the
characters should leave with the definite sense that to
cross him again would be a very, very bad idea. As they
leave, the sounds of Callie's whimpers and Glynnis's

cream sing in concordance with the wind.

If they characters do not decide to tell him every-
thing, he will begin to influence them, though pain or

persuasion, to tell him everything. He is aware of most of
the details already, including why Glynnis wants the
journal, and thus is
character even insinuates she read the journal, he will set

just looking for a confession. If any

that person's mind on fire and stab him through with a
chimerical sword, ensuring that knowledge of the Immor-
tal Eyes remains with him alone. Any other character who
tries to stop him will receive the same treatment. It is
obvious he does not care what the characters opinions are,
though he would much rather have them working for him
than against him. Ultimately, he tries to win the charac-
ters' loyalty, and if he cannot have that, he will give their
names to the Dauntain to be dealt with later.

If this is the ending your character's choose, they
should leave feeling used. Though they thought they
followed their instructions to the letter, they were pawns.

They were used to try and gain more power, and it failed.

Scene Three: Alcernacive Ending

If the character's seek out Prince Yrtalien, he can be
found in his study, talking quietly with someone. The
characters are made to wait about 10 minutes before being
a dark-skinned man walks out of the room, and the
characters are beckoned to enter. The room is much the
same as before; nothing looks out of order. Prince Yrtalien
is seated in a high-backed chair, and he offers the charac-
ters a seat and some wine.

He will immediately inquire as to what he can do for
them. He is aware of Glynnis's attempt to try and locate
information about the Eyestones, and is aware that these
are the Kithain she singled out. He is a mixture of amused
and curious as to their presence here, for he assumes he
would have to take care of this problem later.

If the characters try to blackmail the prince, it doesn't
work. He will smile faintly and promptly begin to torture
the offending creature, asking the others if there is any-
thing else. If the characters begin explaining from the
beginning the nights events, he will listen with an atten-
tive ear. He will ask questions such as, "She told you I was

nota true prince?"

" with incredulity and bemusement. The
characters should get the impression the Glynnis is noth-
ing more than an irritated noble. He will listen to the
complete tale, asking if they have his journal with them.
Subtly, he will also try and ascertain if any have read any
of the entries. If they have not, they have nothing to fear.

Prince Yrtalien will thank them for their honesty and
reward them all with titles. He will give each person a
token of his esteem or offer some more wine, there by
enchanting each character to him. They will leave minus
the diary and feeling very good about their wonderful host.
Hours later Lady Glynnis and Prince Yrtalien ate nowhere
to be found, but screams emanate from his bedroom door.
