Chapcer Seven: Scenes


The Menehune are related to the Nunnehi, a large

group of fae closely tied to the indigenous cultures of
hunter-gatherer humans. They have refused to change
with the rest of the world, bravely resisting modernity and
all its Banality. They cling to the few native cultures who
still eke out traditional lives around the world, in the
distant jungles or mountains not yet trammeled by

technogical society.

The Menehune are native to the South Pacific, the
children of the Polynesians' dreams. They can be found on
Easter Island, Tahiti and especially on Hawai'i. They have
close cousins on New Zealand and New Guinea.

Like all the Nunnehi, regardless of culture or family,
the Menehune are cut off from the Dreaming to a more
drastic degree than the Western changelings. They can no

longer gain any Glamour from it whatsoever and must rely
instead on the Glamour of nature and the spirit world.

When they first realized their entrapment in the
world, they sought aid from spirits, whom they believed to
be the remnants of an older, very powerful dream. Some
claim spirits are the dreams of Gaia, while others claim
they are the long-forgotten dreams of primitive humans —
oreven the dreams of living humans, denied and repressed,
trapped in a seperate world. Regardless, they allied with
many spirits, usually those of plants and stones, and
through them they can gain some Glamour from the
natural world. Some Menehune can even step into the
spirit world (see below).


CDenehune Character

Creation

The following guidelines are for creating Menehune
characters for use by the Storyteller or player in any
Hawai'ian-based chronicle.

Camp

This replaces Court for Menehune changelings. Be-
cause Menehune fall outside the Seelie/Unseelie framework
of mainstream changeling society, those terms are not rel-
evant to them. Instead, Menehune fall into one of two
camps: Feast and War. These reflect the two natures repre-
sented in their culture. The former represents peaceful,
agrarian behavior associated with the god Lono and other
Earth fertility deities. The latter represents a more violent
aspect, associated with the war god Ku and all the arts of war.

As with Seelie/Unseelie aspects, Menehune can shift
between these two camps and often do. During the four
months of the Makahiki, most Menehune are of the Feast, but
some shift to the War for the other eight months of the year.

Legacy

Like other changelings, Menehune characters have
dual Legacies — one to reflect their Feast nature, the other

to represent their War-nature. Common Feast Legacies
include Chief (similar to Regent), Healer (Saint), Farmer
(Bumpkin), Crafter, and Wise One (Sage). War Legacies
include Warrior (Paladin), Hoarder (Rogue), Outcast
(Outlaw, Wretch or Grotesque), Raider (Savage or Beast),
and Wanderer (Wayfarer).

Seeming

Menehune have the same three age-related seemings
as other changelings, but they refer to childling as keiki iki,
wilders as kanaka and gramps as kumu

Calling

Instead of being divided into kith, as the Western
changeling are, the Menehune follow social divisions.
Since each Menehune is born into a particular calling
(choice has nothing to do with it), a Menehune's birth
calling is considered divinely ordained and unchangeable.
Unlike Western fae society, the Menehune have never
suffered societal upheaval or dissent over their customs. In
other words, there is still a clear separation between nobles
and commoners.

Thenoblesare the ali'iand the kahuna, while the hana
and the kokua are commoners (Maka'ainana).


Like the sidhe, ali'i are born to rule. Unlike the sidhe,
they rarely let this go to their heads. They are fair and wise
rulers, realizing fully the circle of life and the contributions
of commoners. The ali'i come from one of the royal
bloodlines that once produced Menehune kings on each
island. Kamehameha's empire never reached the
Menehune, and they were never forcibly united under one
king. They now willingly recognize one chief above all
others, usually the representative of Kaua'i's traditional
bloodline. But sub-chiefs can come from the royal lines of
O'ahu, Maui, Moloka'i and Hawai'i. There is no royal line
from Lana'i.

Each village has a chief. Today, there is only one
village, and so all ali'i except the chief of that village have
become sub-chiefs, advisors to the head chief. However,
mysteriously, fewer and fewer ali'i have been born to new
generations (unlike the sidhe, the ali'ibecame changelings
with the rest of their people long ago).

The ali'i are bearers of the Menehune's Glamour,
which they call mana. Instead of balefire, ceremonies and
feasts during the yearly Malahiki games invest theali'i with
Glamour, which they apportion to the people throughout
the year until the next Malahiki.

Appearance

Like sidhe, ali'i are beautiful people. Their complex-
ions are smooth, and their skin golden or deep brown.
Their teeth are brilliant white and shining, and their
smiles wide and happy. Unlike the sidhe, their laughter is
full and hearty with no hint of sadness. Most male ali'i are
well-muscled and proportioned as warriors while female
alii can be portly. They usually wear feather cloaks.

Seemings

¢ Keiki iki are bright and happy. All their needs are
seen to, and they want for nothing. While some can be
tempermental, it is rare.

© Kanaka are boastful and competitive. They are just
coming into their responsibilities and look forward to
them (unlike many Western fae), but they playfully test
others around them, seeking to hone their own skills of
leadership.

¢ Kumu are mature and regal. They are expected to
lead their people well, and they usually take this seriously.
But this maturity does not mean the death of dreams and
magic, for the ali' iis in charge of ensuring the people never
know a lack of Glamour. Many do succumb toa sadness at
the people's current state of affairs, but a bout of surfing
usually dispels this.

Lifescyles

Allali'i hold influence over their people, even if they
are sub-chiefs. They are expected to advise the high chief
and lead by example. They keep themselves socially sepa-
rate from the commoners, but this is more to reinforce
their magical purity rather than from a sense of disdain.

Affinicy

Fae

Birchrights

© Awe and Beauty — As the sidhe birthright.

© Glamour Vessel — Ali'i can hold quadruple their
normal Glamour rating in temporary points. These points
must be invested into the ali'i from other Menehune. This
is done only during the annual Malahiki fea: ticipat-
ing Menehune spend temporary points, and they are
"stored" by the chosen ali'i. The alii cannot use these
points himself; instead, other Menehune can draw from
this well of Glamour to fuel their cantrips (or any other
use). The Menehune can only do so with the permission
of the ali'i, and they must be within 50 feet of him.


Lralcies

 Banality's Curse — Like the sidhe frailty.

 Sacrosanct— Since Menehune do not have balefire
toenliven their freeholds, the ali'i's stored Glamour is very
important to get them through banal times. If Banality
ever effects an ali'i, much of this stored Glamour is de-
stroyed (five points per point of Banality the ali'i gains).
Thus, alii must be wary.

Stepping on anali''s shadow will destroy one point of
Glamour (stored Glamour first, then the ali'i's own Glam-
our), and for this reason, it is taboo. Also, when an ali'i
walks pasta commoner, his retinue will blow conch horns.
Any commoner who does not bow before the ali'i destroys
one point of Glamour; this is also taboo.

"You dare come before me like this? You are from far
lands and have strange ways, but this does not excuse your
rudeness. Bow now, and then we will talk."

RRATWAT

The kahunas are the mystical lore-keepers of the
Menehune. Their wisdom is vitally important to the
Menehune, moreso these days than in times past, for they
are the intermediaries between the spirits and the people.
While each Menehune may have an alliance with a
particular totem, the kahunas are necessary to make tribal
and place-specific alliances, to ordain or abandon he' iaus
as necessary, and to divine bad omens from the spirit
world.

The Menehune system of taboos is regulated by the
kahunas. Using evidence from the spirit world or from
other divinations, they can agree to change the taboos
within a given year (unlike with traditional Hawai'ians).
Only if a majority of kahunas agree will these new taboos
be announced. To announce one without consensus risks
people following the new taboo and thus breaking old
taboos — a cycle of bad luck is begun.

A kahuna also knows how to appease the spirits when
taboos are broken. In the past, the spirits would often
require the death of the perpetrator, even if it was a
Menehune. But in these times of dwindling population,
the kahunas are hesitant to do so. They have so far found
other sacrifices to appease the spirits.

Kahunas often spend timing gathering lore in particu-
lar areas, whether it be astrology, plant lore, animal lore or
whatever other field of knowledge would be useful in
interpreting the needs of the spirits.

Appearance

Kahunas come in many physical varieties: short, tall,
fat, thin. Their eyes are what set them apart, for the stars
are reflected in them. In the dark, their eyes will shine with
the light of the stars that they have gazed on so deeply.
They usually wear robes or other ceremonial clothing.

Seemings

© Keiki iki are different from normal children. They
go off by themsel
waves and the trees. They feel a calling that they cannot
put words to yet.

and stare for hours at the stars, the

© Kanaka are questioning. They will ask "why" of
many things (careful, however, not to break taboo in
doing so).

© Kumu are calmer and know their place in life.
Many of their questions have been answered, and they
spend the rest of their days knowing more fully what they
already know.

Lifescyles

Kahunas like to seek out sacred or naturally pure
places to mediate. It is in these quiet places that nature and
the gods show their wills. Wisdom can come in many
forms: the leap of a fish, the fall of the rain on palm leaves,
the dance of a bird in the morning. A kahuna is ever-
watchful for the omens all about her.

Affinicy

Nature

Birchrighzs

* Break Taboo — A kahuna may break a taboo and
get away with it. This may only be done once per month
and must not be done with disrespect. There must be a
good reason to break the taboo. The kahuna spends one
Glamour point; if she does not, then Kapu'akua (see
Chapter Two) will chase her.

© Spirit Speech — All kahuna can speak with spirits
and understand their language. Other Menehune can only
understand their particular totems, but the kahuna can
speak and listen to all spirits.

Like boggans or nockers, the hanaare the craftspeople
of the Menehune. It is they who built the famous plat-
forms, ditches and he'iau scattered throughout the islands
that so greatly puzzle archaeologists. Despite their name,
farmers and common fishers are also members of this

ling, which make up the most numerous of the
Menehune. Their many crafts include not just structures,
but canoes, cloaks, leis, weapons, ete.

Hana are always busy with some project, and they
often work together in groups. One hana may have singing
or poetry as her craft and will practice this while others
work around her, providing musical accompaniment to
the daily chores.

And there are many chores. The Menehune live in a
subsistence culture, and besides gathering theirneeds from

the environment, they must spend time with humans who

follow the old ways, teaching these humans not to forget.

The hana are the heart of the Menehune. Without
them, chiefs, priests and warriors would be useless. Why
rule an empty village? Why propitiate the spirits when no
one has angered them? Who is there to fight for without
the hana?

But this fact is often forgotten by the other callings,
and the hana must patiently remind them, usually through
pranks. It is not against taboo to disassemble the high
kahuna's grass hut around himas he sleeps, nor to serve the
chief bitter fruit. Likewise, when a warrior's tunic rips too
easily (and embarassingly) or his surfboard cracks, tum-
bling him into the sea, it is not against any law.

Appearance

Not unlike boggans, hana are most often portly and
short. They are a jolly people, content for the most part
with their lot in life. They are social and work well
together, except for kokua, who they distrust. Most often,
they can be found wearing traditional Hawai'ian clothing

Seemings
° Kei

things and playing with them, trying to figure them out

ki are playful and curious, always picking up

© Kanaka are dedicated and ready to throw them-
selves into the task as hand. During this time, hana choose
one craft to specialize in.

© Kumu are masters of their chosen craft and are well
regarded for it by all. They are ready to relax in this phase
of life and tutor younger hana.

Lifescyles

Hana can be found wherever their craft takes them:
searching the forests for materials, carving canoes on the
shore, collecting flowers for leis, stoking up a fire for
roasting pigs, or just about any other activity that makes up
the life of a traditional Hawaiian commoner.

Affinicy

Prop


Birchrights

© Craftwork — Similar to the boggan birthright.
When hana work together, they can build just about any
traditional structure in one night, as long as they are not
witnessed by any banal observers.

Fraitcies

© Abandonment — If for some reason a hana cannot
finish his task in the time he declares at the start of the
task, he will leave it uncompleted and never return to it.
Any other hana who attempts to finish it risks suffering
Banality.

Kokua are the warriors of the Menehune, those who
are born to defend the people from their enemies. While
in the past their enemies were often other Menehune
villages, today the kokua guard against humans and West-
ern fae. It is a hard job and requires long hours of patience
when on guard duty or when watching humans from afar.
For this reason, kokua play hard when off duty, choosing
sports or activities that hone athletic skills.

Surfing (he'enalu, or "sliding on a wave") is a favorite
of theirs. Among ancient Hawai'ians, this sport was re-
served for kings, but it was too popular among the kokua to
be declared taboo among them. So, kokua can often be
found mixing with mortals on surfing beaches, searching
for the highest waves.

A kokua is not necessarily of the War camp, for they
can be defenders of the peace and the fields as well as
soldiers. In the past, many warriors would ally with fish
totems, such as Shark, rather than plants. But the scarcity
of these sea animals of late has caused many Menehune
kokua to instead ally with rock totems.

Most kokua use clubs as their weapons, but the hon-
ored among them sometimes have shark-tooth swords
(especially those whostill follow Shark). (These swords do
Strength +2 in damage.)

Appearance

Kokua are physically fit and look it. They appear to be
perfect physical specimens. They often wear only a loose
tunic (both males and females) — the better to show off
their tatoos.

Seemings:

¢ Keikiiki are boisterous and competitive. They fight
with other kokua to see who is the best at everything.

 Kanaka are wild but more disciplined than when
younger. They know the penalties for not following the
ali''s orders, but can still sometimes forget.

¢ Kumu are mature, disciplined and deadly. Their
battle skills are well-honed but they are less energetic,
preferring sometimes to go fishing rather than fighting.

L esctyles

Kokua form small societies or groups, and one in each
group rises as the natural leader — usually the best athelete
among them. These groups often fight with each other,
sometimes in moc' sometimes in real wars, as some-
one gets angry and can't control himself. If this is forbidden
by the alii (which is onl
way, all who fight are considered to have broken taboo.

‘Aumakua(Tocems)

Each Menehune has a spiritual connection with a
totem spirit. Their close ties to nature have granted them
the ability to contact the totems of plants (including
trees), rocks and bodies of water. Typical Hawai'ian to-
tems include palm trees, Mokihana berries and trees, ‘o'hio
trees, lava, waterfalls, etc. Examples of some totems are
given below (see "Menehune Totems").

Contacting a totem spirit marks the "coming-of-age"
of a Menehune. By the time a Menehune is aware of her
faerie nature, she has usually received some indication of
the identity of her totem — either through a dream or
visionquest or by frequent contact with physical manifes-
tations of the totem.

For example, as a kahuna keiki iki, Rushing Water
became lost in the forest after a volcanic eruption, separat-
ing her from her friends. When her family found her,
Rushing Water was sleeping peacefully beneath the shel-
ter ofa ‘o'hio tree. Later, Rushing Water dreamed of taking
a trip in a beautiful ‘o'hio wood-carved canoe. These
occurrences seemed to indicate to Rushing Water and to
the elders of her village that she had an affinity with the
‘O‘hio totem.

AMenehune preparing tocontacther totem spirit for
the first time must prepare herself with a hula and luau,
chanting and giving thanks to the spirit. The Menehune
then places herself in the presence of a physical represen-
tation of her totem. A kahuna (usually one with the same
totem or whose totem is also physically manifested in the
chosen location) then steps sideways, taking the aspirant
with her into the Umbra (see below). Once there, the
Menehune seeking contact must chant to the totem to
draw it to her.

Totem alliance is "purchased" through a new Back-
ground Trait: Totem:

Menehune gain the following advantages from a
totem alliance:

¢ A Menehune'salliance with a totem is necessary for
her to be able to enter the Umbra; without it, she cannot
step sideways, no matter her Arts or Realms.

¢ A Menehune gains certain adjustments to her
Advantages and/or Abilities, depending on the totem she
allies with (see the description of the particular totem).

© The totem comes in the form ofa relationship with
the totem spirit itself, practiced through stewardship of
the totem's material children (palm trees for the Palm
totem, lava flows for the Lava totem, etc.).

The Gaunclec

The Gauntlet is an invisible barrier that
separates our world from the world of spirit —
also known as the Umbra. The gauntlet is in a
sense related to Banality in that it is thicker in
some places and thinner in others. It is at its
thickest in places where science and technology
hold sway (cities, industrial parks, waste dumps)
and thinnest in natural places (forest glades,
virgin forests, high mountain peaks). The thicker
the Gauntlet, the harder it is for one to enter the
spirit world at that point.

Stepping Sideways

Menehune with totem alliances (there are few with-
out one) can step sideways into the Umbra. This requires
Wayfare 3 (Portal Passage) or higher and Nature 2 (Ver-
dant Forest). The Menehune must be in the presence of
her totem material (lava for the Lava totem, etc.). The
Menehune "walks into" her totem material — by stepping
ina river, plunging intoa stand of palm trees, or disappear-
ing into a molten lava flow.

ABunk must be performed, but the number of successes
is not automatic; the player must roll dice to see if his
character succeeds or not, and then the maximum number
ofsuccessis limited by the Bunk played. Thus, the Menehune
rolls Wits (for Wayfare) + Mythlore (for Nature). The
difficulty for this passage is equal to the Gauntlet (see
below), the wall between the worlds. However, this diffi
culty is adjusted according to the relative purity of the
Menehune's totem material. Impure materials add one to
three to the difficulty, depending on how tainted the mate-
rials are. Pure materials likewise subtract one to three from
the difficulty, depending on how clean the materials are.

For instance, Big Stick of the Menehune finds himself
in Honolulu and wishes to enter the Umbra. His totem is
Palm, so he finds a palm tree along the crowded beaches.
It has grown up "breathing" car smog and is somewhat
wilted. The Gauntlet is eight here, and the Storyteller

adds two to Big Stick's difficulty due to the impure totem

material. Big Stick's difficulty is 10 — it's almost impos-
sible for him to cross over here.

‘A Menehune can bring other changelings into the
Umbra with him. He must have the Fae Realm of the
appropriate level (1 for commoners, 2 for nobles) and
spend one Glamour point for every person brought over.
A\ll those stepping sideways must hold hands.

"Caught" means that the Menehune is tem-
porarily suspended between the physical world
and the Umbra. She cannot move until assisted
by another Menehune who can step sideways or
a Garou. Although the Menehune can neither
beseen nor be attacked by physical denizens, evil
spirits wander the Gauntlet looking for such
trapped spirit travelers. After an hour has passed,
the Menehune can again try to complete the
travel. If that fails, he cannot leave on his own.
Ifhe is not found and pulled through by another
Menehune or Garou, he will be caught forever.

A changeling who cannot step sideways may find
himself caught in the Umbra ifhis guide leaves him. In this
case, he may search out a trod (an ancient faerie path in
the spirit world) and return to the physical world from
there. But this is a long and dangerous task.


The Menehune's ability to enter the Umbra provides
them with many advantages. Banality is rare in the Um-
bra, usually only prevalent around areas of high Gauntlet.

While in the Umbra, Menehune can "peek" into the
physical world by rolling their Glamour against the Gaunt-
let of the area.

Ancient trods exist in the Umbra, old spirit realms
and domains of faerie power from before the gates to
Arcadia closed. These have been empty for many centu-
ties, unvisited by the fae. Some Menehune have sought
these places out and use them to gain Glamour or expunge
Banality, allowing them a connection to the Dreaming
they otherwise do not have. However, the journey to these
far off trods is usually fraught with danger, for many evil
spirits see changelings as a tasty snack.

Abdilicies

New Talents for Menehune include Swimming and
Throwing. Skills include Animal Ken, Canoeing, Climbing,
Dancing (hula or otherwise), Fishing, Herbalism, Hunting,
Meditation, Singing, and Surfing. Knowledges include Ani-
mal Lore, Area Knowledge, Plant Lore, Spirit Lore and
Traditions. Menehune do not usually possess modern Abili-
ties such as Streetwise, Drive, Computer and Science.

Backgrounds

With the exception of Title, Menehune characters
may have any of the standard changeling Backgrounds. In
addition, Menehune characters may possess the Back-
ground: Familiar Spirit, which gives a bond of friendship
withan Umbralspirit, usually an animal. (See The Werewolf
Players Guide for a description of this Background.)

Arcs

Although Menehune characters may possess any of
the standard changeling Arts, they are more apt to special-
ize in Primal, Soothsay and Wayfare.

Realms

Menehune magic affects the same realms as the magic
of standard changelings

following list of Bunks is arranged by the Art to which they
are most closely affiliated, although any Bunk can be effec-
tive to invoke the use of any Art. The Storyteller should feel
free to create additional Bunks for Menehune characters.

Glamour and Banalicy

Because they are able to tap the natural world for
Glamour, Menehune tend to have slightly higher levels of
beginning Glamour than other changelings; the Story-
teller should award one additional dot of Glamour to her
Menehune characters. Conversely, they are more susce
tible to Banality. When away from natural settings, difficulty
factors for enchanting others are increased by one.

Gachering Glamour

Since they are severed from the Dreaming, Menehune
cannot easily gather Glamour from human creativity
(difficulties are raised by two, unless the activity is from an
indigenous culture, such as a Hawai'ian traditional hula
dance or uma wrestling match). Instead, they mainly draw
Glamour from Gaia Herself. A Menehune's current Legacy
determines the way in which she replenishes her supply of
Glamour. Feast People gather Glamour from natural phe-
nomenon, such as trees and rocks, while War People get
theirs from animals, especially hunting animals like pigs or
fish. A pig hunt among young Menehune War People is

sure to bring much Glamour (as will a pig hunt by native

Hawai'ian park rangers trying to control the boar popula-
tion by hunting). All Menehune may gather Glamour

from pure water (through Harvesting, below). In addition,
ali'i may gather Glamour from the bones or other physical
remains of dead (perhaps slain) chieftains or other power-
ful people (which includes movie stars or politicians). The
bones will provide a certain amount of Glamour over a
number of years (similar to dross) as long as they are
ritually kept and are not seen or touched by mortals.

As with other changelings, Glamour may be obtained
by Menehune in one of three ways.

Harvescing

This slow method of gathering Glamour is the
Menehune equivalent of Reverie. In order fora Menehune
to use this means of refreshing her supply of Glamour, she
must locate a naturally occurring source. In general, it is
not possible for Menehune to gather Glamour within the
confines ofa city, even when in the presence of a possible
source. Plants grown in hothouses or cultivated gardens,
Christmas tree farms, rock gardens or rivers flowing through
the center of a city do not provide Glamour sources for
Menehunesince they are usually so influenced by Banality
or simply too tainted.

System: Once she has located her source, the
Menehune must spend at least one hour in contact with
the source (dangling her feet or fingers ina flowing stream,


sitting at the foot of or in the branches of a tree, climbing
or sitting upon a rock or inside a stone cave, or relaxing in
a field of flowers). The Menehune character then rolls
Wits + Kenning (difficulty 7). One point of Glamour may
be gathered for each success, provided the Menehune has
spent at least one hour per success surrounded by her
Glamour source. This process may only occur once per day
and the same source may not be used more than once per
moon's phase (i.e., a maximum of two times per month).

Raiding

Alternatively, a Menehune may attempt torip Glam-
our from a natural source. This process, known as Raiding,
is the Menehune version of Ravaging. Although doing so
reduces the amount of time that must be dedicated to the
process, a Menehune using this method also runs the risk
of increasing her Banality.

System: The Menehune must be somewhat familiar
with the source from which she intends to wrest Glamour.
She rolls her Banality rating (difficulty 6). The number of
successes equals the number of points of Glamour gained.
A botch gives the Menehune a permanent point of Banal-
ity and may harm the subject of the Raiding in some way:
a living plant may die, a body of water may become
polluted, etc.

Blessing

This is the Menehune method of achieving Rapture.

The process of Rapture allows a changeling to receive
Glamour froma work of herown creation. Since Menehune
cannot inspire themselves in this manner, they have
discovered a way to use their connection with the Umbra
toachieve a similar ecstasy through the blessing of a totem
spirit. This may only be attempted at the changing of the
seasons (four times a year).

System: The Menehune must first undergo a ritual
purification. When she is ready, she attempts to summon
her totem spirit by offering it a song, story, dance, lu'au or
other artistic form. The totem spirit will usually answer
such a summons, although it will remain in the Umbra
nearby. When the spirit is present, the Menehune rolls the
appropriate Attribute + Ability score for her gift to the
spirit (difficulty 7). The number of succes
number of Glamour points gained directly from the totem

s indicates the

spirit. Five successes awards the Menehune a permanent
point of Glamour. A botch causes the spirit to flee and
gives the changeling two points of temporary Banality.
The Menehune may not try again for a Blessing until the
next season change.

CDenchune Tozems

The spirits of plants, minerals and the elements are
frequently willing to adopt Menehune as their charges. It
is this relationship with these Umbral beings that enables
Menehune to step sideways. The totem spirits detailed
below should give Storytellers ideas for designing their
own Menehune totems for use in Hawai'ian chronicles
Menehune may ally with any Garou totem (at half
the Background Cost). However, it is rare for them to
choose animal totems, since they would then have to be in

the presence of that animal to enter the Umbra.

(Dokiham

Mokihani is a beautiful tree and berry totem. Her
perfume makes everything she touches beautiful. What
nds the

Ban: Mokihani requires her children to protect her
trees. Children of the Mokihani must never use leis or other
adornments without rubbing her berries onto them first.

Lava

Background Cost: 4 (Garou 7)

Lava is the maker of the world. Her substance will one
day become the hard rock of the earth. But that is in the
future; for now, Lava is fluid and mobile, perhaps the only
rock totem that understands change and movement. She
is a hot totem, coming so recently from Gaia's womb, and
can cough out clouds of gas she brings with her.

Traits: Lava grants her Menehune the ability to
shapeshift into molten lava. This amazing ability costs the
Menehune one Glamour point per turn he is in this shape.
While molten, the Menehune can flow into cracks and he
is seeringly hot; he will ignite anything flammable over
which he flow

(Garou gain a Gift that allows them a similar power;
it is called Gaia's Blood.)

Ban: Lava demands that her children never flee from
an enemy but keep moving onward — inexorably, unstop-
pable,

Prelude — November 5, 1995
Yrtalien and Glynnis leave San Francisco for a desti-
nation in the "west." (Although it is not stated, they are,

in fact, going to Hawaii.)

Chapter One — December 1, 1995

1. The characters meet at the Toybox Coffee Shop.
Leigh is the last to join them, informing them that Duke
Aeon wishes to meet with them at their "earliest conve-
nience."

2. The group travels to the duke's palace, where Aeon
himself greets them at the door.

3. Aeon tells the group that he has received word that
more information concerning their quest lies with a group
of kithain north of San Francisco, near Point Reyes.
Morgan has a waking dream in which two swanlike boats
—one black and one white— pursue each other across the
sea. Rasputin intimates that this may be the beginning of
a longer journey.

Chapter Two — December 2, 1995

1. Fizzlewig holds an early Yule celebration for the
group.

2. Cyprian Ryder (also known as Chevalier) finds a
book which leads him to make contact with a woman
named Signe Henderson. Asa result, his memories return.

3. The characters exchange gifts — some of which
will be significant to them in the future. In particular,
Morgan's gift to Tor is a small photo album of photographs
of herself and her parents during the period of Tor's
banishment from the Daniels family.


4. Glynnis and Yrtalien anticipate the eventual ar-
rival of the group — and Yrtalien expresses his hope that
he can win them to his cause.

5. The group heads north along Highway 1, straight
intoan ambush by Blade anda group of obviously Unseelie
kithain. They are nearly defeated and Tor is almost lost to
Banality, but are rescued by a number of strange kithain
whom Rasputin suspects are selkies.

Eyestones. She also tells of the sinking of the Isle of
Dreams, the dispersal of the stones and the sacrifice of the
queen of the selkies. She tells the companions that the
Shadowstone resides with the Menehune — the native
kithain of Hawaii.

Court of Shadows. Glynnis' private thoughts reveal that

‘once again to Arcadia.

A brief history of the arrival of the kithain in Hawaii.

Chapter Five — (no date is given, the characters are

December 3 — 4, 1995)

Chapter Nine — December 11, 1995

1. The Menehune get ready to take the companions
back to the swanship in the grotto. Leigh's jealousy at
Valmont's obvious attraction to Lulani flares briefly. Chief
Makani explains about the native belief that it is bad luck
for anyone's shadow to fall upon their chief. Leigh associ-
ates the Menehune concept of shadow with Banality.

2. Ryder and his two companions encounter Lord
Devlin who brings them to Yrtalien's palace.

3. The companions go to the grotto, where their
swanship is waiting. The Menehune bring out one of their
double canoes to accompany their new friends part way on
their journey to the Big Island. Morgan frees her chimera
before she leaves. Chief Makani opens a sea trod and they
set sail. Before they reach their destination, the Menehune
double back and return to their home. The companions
land on the island of Hawai'i —on a black sand beach.

Edmund learns about volcanos. Valmont uses his eshu gift
of direction to lead the companions to their destination —
wherever that may be.

4. Yrtalien and Glynnis try to find out more about the
Shadowstone and its companion gems from Kanani. They
are interrupted by the arrival of visiting kithain.

5. The companions get lost in the tropical wilderness
Stopping just before nightfall to prepare a meal, they are
approached by a wizened old native woman whoshares food
with them and then warns them not tostay overnight in the
area, telling them that toxic fumes from Kilauea, the nearby
volcano, might be dangerous to them. She tells them how
to find a road that will take them to Hilo. The companions
follow her directions and get a lift to the city in a pickup
truck, where they find rooms at the Seacrest Bed and
Breakfast (the same hotel where Vargas also has a room).

6. Ryder and Yrtalien meet. Ryder realizes that he is in
the presence of the Unseelie kithain, a fact that gives him
faction at the thought of ending their
threat to sanity. When his sapphire, concealed by a leather
half-glove, comes into contact with the Shadowstone,
however, the pain cripples Ryder — in much the same
fashion as it did when he entered the Toybox and came
near the toy chest. Yrtalien recognizes in Ryder a powerful
kithain whom he wishes to cooperate and a
private wing of his palace.

7. Yrtalien wakes with the certainty that Eleighanara
(Leigh) has arrived in Hilo.

Chapter Ten — December 12, 1995

1. At their hotel, the companions have breakfast and
make plans. They learn from their waiter that the old
woman they met might have been the volcano goddess
Pele, whose appearance often warns of impending volca-
nic activity. They also learn that the place where they
almost spent the night was in the path of a |:

the morning playing "tourist" before they embark on the
rest of their quest. Vargas sees them leave and recognizes
them from Blade's description.

2. Ryder informs his companions that he intends to
attempt to remain in Yrtalien's palace, admitting that his
dreams have indicated that the group they seek will find
their way to the prince's freehold.

3. Yrtalien finds Leigh on the beach and extends an
invitation to her and her companions to visit his freehold.
Leigh remembers a little more about her previous alliance
with Yrtalien in Arcadia and that she once loved the
Foresworn Prince.

4. Ryder slips away from the palace and leaves a
message for Vargas. Then he lets the gem in his palm lead
him back to the freehold.


5. Vargas watches Leigh's meeting with Yrtalien
before returning to his room, where Ryder's message
awaits him.

6. The companions decide to accept Yrtalien's offer,
realizing that they are bearding the lion in his den.

7. Ryder confronts Yrtalien, and the prince reveals to the
Dauntain that he knows about Ryder's gem. Yrtalien tells
Ryder that someone else bearing a similar gem is on her way
to the freehold. Yrtalien promises not to reveal Ryder's
presence in the freehold to the bearer of the third gem — with
the tacit understanding that Ryder is now in Yrtalien's debt.

8. The companions discuss shadows, Banality and
Unseelie philosophy as they make their way to Yrtalien's
freehold.

9. Yrtalien tortures Glynnis with chimeric torments
in order to find out if she knows anything more about the
Eyestones. His game is interrupted by the arrival of Leigh
and her companions.

Chapter Eleven — December 13 — 21, 1995

1. Valmont talks with Kanani and begins to suspect
Yrtalien's dark purpose in bringing her to his court. He
decides to share his knowledge with the "adults" in his group.

2. Morgan again writes in her diary, chronicling her
group's attempts to assimilate themselves into Yrtalien's
court. She mentions that Yrtalien is keeping company with
Leigh, Valmont is spending time with Kanani, Rasputin is
mingling with people but not getting close to any in
particular, and she has attracted Glynnis's attention be-
cause of their common affiliation with House Eiluned. She
expresses her worries about Tor, who seems out of sorts in
the freehold and simply states that Edmund is doing fine.
Glynnis visits Morgan in the childling's room and tries to
gether to "borrow" the Keystone from Leigh so thatshe can
help Morgan learn how to use it to increase the effects of
her Glamour. Morgan has a vision tempting her to power.

3. Ryder contemplates the bargain he struck with
Yrtalien, who demonstrated his ability to use the
Shadowstone to relieve — at least temporarily — Ryder's
nearly constant pain. Having deduced that Ryder and his
companionsare Dauntain, Yrtalien has promised Ryderall

xcept for Leigh in return for Ryder's nce.
to Ryder his plans for the sacrifice at the

upcoming Winter Solstice.

4. Rasputin and Signe meet on Yrtalien's private beach.
Signe inadvertently reminds Rasputin of his traumatic child-
hood and gets rare glimpse at the frightened person behind
the pooka's carefully lighthearted facade. Signe begins to
wonder whether "reality" is a cure for everyone.

5. Devlin tries to get Tor to participate in ravaging to
reclaim some of his lost Glamour.

Appendix: The

Jenehune


Later, Tor is rebuffed by Diana (a fellow troll besides
being one of the Dauntain) who accuses him of being a
ravager of human creativity.

6. Yrtalien makes his bid for Leigh's loyalty — and
loses. He accuses her of breaking her oath to him, made
long ago in Arcadia, and professes his continuing love for
her. They declare a civilized sort of war on each other —
with the gemstones as prizes — and before they part

company Yrtalien lets drop a hint that something will

happen during his Winter Solstice ceremony that will
increase his power and solidify his position as the head of
his Court of Shadows. Leigh remembers Valmont's suspi-
cions about Yrtalien's intentions to sacrifice Kanani and
begins to believe that they might be true. When she later
confronts Valmont, after he has had his own meeting with
Yrtalien, the eshu denies having any such dark intuitions.

7. Edmund admires his new suit of chimeric armor —a
gift from Yrtalien — and confides in Mr. Dumpy that
Yrtalien has promised to make him a knight and give hima
horse as soon as he does something to prove his worthiness.

8. Ryder awakens in agony from the pain in his hand
and realizes that Yrtalien not only has the power to remove
his suffering but to augment it as well. Despite his best
efforts, he is forced to seek out Yrtalien and beg the prince
to take away his pain. Yrtalien does so, but makes it clear
that he now commands Ryder's obedience. He also in-
forms Ryder that he has changed his mind and is willing to
give him Eleighnara along with the other oathmates.

Chapter Twelve — December 22, 1995 (the long-
est night)

1. The great beast that dreams at the heart of the
volcano known as Kilauea stirs restlessly in her slumber,
only vaguely aware of the events that are about to transpire.

2. The morning of the Winter Solstice brings a "gift"
of chimeric snow. Edmund, Rasputin and Morgan have a
snowball fight before Rasputin takes the two childlings to
a meeting of the group

3. Despite the absence of Valmont, Leigh tells her
oathmates of her fear that Valmont's early suspicions about
Yrtalien were correct. Leigh announces that Yrtalien tried to
enlist her in his cause and that she turned him down. Morgan
relates Glynnis' attempt to entice her into "borrowing" the
Keystone from Leigh. Tor tells how Devlin tried to convince
Tor that ravaging was a good way for him to augment his
dwindling reserves of Glamour. Leigh confesses that she had
hoped to win Yrtalien over to the group's quest. Rasputin
comments on Edmund's uncharacteristic silence. The com-
panions discuss the possibility that Yrtalien might be planning
to sacrifice Kanani, and Leigh and Rasputin speak of the
long-forgotten practice of the faerie "tithe" to the world of
the dead. Leigh admits that Kanani cannot be found and that


she, Rasputin and Tor have been searching for her. Valmont
arrives, and Morgan notices that the eshu is wearing a
circular onyx pin. Valmont says that Yrtalien had given it to
him the night before, saying that it wasa gift to Valmont from
Kanani. Leigh realizes that Yrtalien has used the pin to
ensorcel Valmontand has Tor remove it from the eshu. Once
it is removed, the enchantment is broken and Valmont
remembers his concern for Kanani's safety. Before the com-
panions set out in search of Kanani, Leigh confesses that she
inadvertently confirmed for Yrtalien that there were four

Eyestones and that they could be used to open Silver's Gate.

4. Ryder meets with Vargas in Hilo, and the two men

make plans to ambush Leigh's group at the place of

freehold nearly deserted. Finally a hung-over nocker informs
them that the prince and the rest of his followers have gone
to "the volcano." Valmont realizes that he knows exactly
where the group needs to be — and that he had not, in fact,
gotten his companions lost when they first arrived on the
island of Hawai'i. He uses his Glamour to transport the group
tothe spot where they met the old woman—almost certainly
amanifestation of the volcano goddess Pele. From there, they
head toward Kilauea, hoping they will arrive in time.

7. The companions arrive on the scene, but a loud
comment from Edmund destroys their hope for secrecy
Valmont makes a desperate charge toward the troll body-

moment, Ryder and his Dauntain ambush the characters.

8. A complicated battle takes place between the
Dauntain and the characters. Valmont concentrates on
rescuing Kanani — and is unexpectedly aided by Signe.
Ryder attacks Morgan, but Tor intervenes. Rasputin drags
Morgan away from the battle. Leigh battles Diana. Edmund
comes to her aid, but his sword shears through the strings
holding the pouch containing the Keystone. He retrieves
it and runs off to help Tor in his fight.

Vargas opens fire on Yrtalien and Glynnis. Yrtalien uses
the Shadowstone to transport himself and Glynnis to safety.
Diana defeats Leigh and chains her in iron manacles before
advancing on Tor. Ryder and Tor trade blows until they are

9. Deprived of his opportunity to capture or kill
Yrtalien, Vargas turns his attentions to Rasputin and
Morgan — who surrender to him rather than risk being
shot by the fanatic Dauntain.

10. Yrtalien realizes that he has been betrayed by the
Dauntain and again uses the Shadowstone to intensify the
pain in Ryder's palm. Ryder is crippled by the sudden flare
of agony in his hand. Tor breaks off the fight. Seeing his
opponent in such great pain, Tor offers him the only mercy
he can think of. Ryder allows Tor to sever the hand
containing the sapphire from his arm. Edmund snatches up
the severed hand and runs off. In a moment of sudden
despair, realizing that he has lived only for the hunt, Ryder
throws himself into the lava — Tor cannot stop him in
time. Diana arrives in time to capture a spiritless Tor. Once
the Dauntain have rounded up the five captured compan-
ions, the group realizes that Edmund is not among them and
that the redcap childling conveniently made off with both
Leigh's stone and the sapphire that was in Ryder's palm.

11. The group is herded into a van. Signe gets in with
them to guard them until they arrive at their destination —
a place where Signe assures the kithain that they will
storing their minds to reality. The group
attempts to convince Signe that she is making a mistake.

eive help in r

Rasputin reminds Signe that reality is not always the best of
all possible worlds. When the van stops and Diana and
Vargas open the back to let their prisoners out, Signe has
been turned by the group. Holding a pistol on her former
companions, she allows the group — now freed of their
manacles — to escape. Then she leaves her former col-
leagues — presumably to return to life as one of the kithain.

12. The companions make their way in the van to
Hilo and take a pair of rooms at a cheap motel. During the
night, Tor wakes and, unable to remember who or where
he is, wanders away from the group.

13. The four remaining oathmates— Leigh, Morgan,
Rasputin and Valmont — make a decision to concentrate
on finding Tor rather than Yrtalien, believing that the
ing that

of the troll. In the midst of her tears, Morgan reveals that

recovery of their friend supersedes their quest. F

the sapphire gem is the Waystone, the third of the four
Immortal Eyes. Morgan also belatedly remembers the
identity of the traitor in her dream — Edmund.

14. Aboard the black swanship, Edmund reminds
Yrtalien of his promise to knight him and give hima horse.
Yrtalien, now in possession of three of the four Eyestones,
puts him off. Edmund begins to regret his actions — but is
consoled by Glynnis, who tells him that Yrtalien uses
everyone for his own purposes.
